## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task seeks the rate law dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t. The rate of change of concentration typically follows power-law dependence on concentration (nth-order kinetics), but may also include time-dependent terms for non-autonomous systems, oscillatory reactions, or reactions with time-varying external inputs.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to concentration squared)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate dependence)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (transition between zero and first order)
- Autocatalytic kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse first-order reactions)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Time-dependent rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate constant)
- Consecutive reaction contribution: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * t * exp(c2 * t) (intermediate species dynamics)
- Fractional-order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (fractional order with constant source/sink)
- Quadratic polynomial in A: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A + c2 (competing reaction pathways)
- Cubic rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A**3 + c1 * A (third-order with first-order contribution)
- Oscillatory modulation: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (periodically driven reaction)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Pure concentration dependence (no explicit t) → autonomous ODE, classical rate law dA/dt = f(A) with power-law or rational forms
- Negative coefficient on A terms → consumption/decay of species A
- Positive constant term in rate law → continuous external source or zeroth-order production
- Product form A*(c-A) → autocatalytic or logistic behavior with a carrying capacity
- Rational dependence on A → enzyme-like or inhibition mechanism from quasi-steady-state approximation of intermediate species
- Explicit time dependence → non-autonomous system, possibly photochemical, temperature-ramped, or externally driven reaction
- Multiple powers of A (e.g., A + A²) → parallel reaction pathways of different orders
- Sign change in dA/dt at specific A values → equilibrium points indicating reversible reactions
